(function(win, doc, style, timeout) {
    var STYLE_ID = 'at-body-style';
  
    function getParent() {
      return doc.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
    }
  
    function addStyle(parent, id, def) {
      if (!parent) {
        return;
      }
  
      var style = doc.createElement('style');
      style.id = id;
      style.innerHTML = def;
      parent.appendChild(style);
    }
  
    function removeStyle(parent, id) {
      if (!parent) {
        return;
      }
  
      var style = doc.getElementById(id);
  
      if (!style) {
        return;
      }
  
      parent.removeChild(style);
    }

    function initFunc() {
        addStyle(getParent(), STYLE_ID, style);
        setTimeout(function() {
            removeStyle(getParent(), STYLE_ID);
        }, timeout);
    }
    window.addEventListener("oneTrustCookieAccepted", function(evt) {
        if(evt.detail.targeting){
            initFunc()
        }

      }
      return null;
  }

      <span>Awareness of the different injection techniques on Linux seems to be relatively low — especially when compared with Windows.</span>
    </div>
  </div>

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-20 title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-4ba4b067ff" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-4ba4b067ff&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:33:10Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Introduction&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Introduction</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pt-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-396ad82c6c&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:36:49Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Process injection techniques are an important part of an attacker&#39;s toolset. They can enable threat actors to run malicious code inside a legitimate process to avoid detection, or to place hooks in remote processes to modify their behavior.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The topic of process injection on Windows machines has been extensively researched, and there is relatively good awareness of it. For Linux machines, this is not exactly the case. Although some great &lt;a href=\&#34;https://jm33.me/process-injection-on-linux.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>resources&lt;/a> have been &lt;a href=\&#34;https://joev.dev/posts/unprivileged-process-injection-techniques-in-linux\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>written&lt;/a> on the &lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.aon.com/cyber-solutions/aon_cyber_labs/linux-based-inter-process-code-injection-without-ptrace2/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>topic&lt;/a>, awareness of the different injection techniques on Linux seems to be relatively low — especially when compared with Windows.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We drew inspiration from a &lt;a href=\&#34;https://i.blackhat.com/USA-19/Thursday/us-19-Kotler-Process-Injection-Techniques-Gotta-Catch-Them-All-wp.pdf?_gl=1*ci4ouq*_gcl_au*MTEyMTMyMTU4NC4xNzMwNjE1NzMw*_ga*MjYwMDA3OTU3LjE2ODk2ODg0MDQ.*_ga_K4JK67TFYV*MTczMDYxNTczMC4yNzQuMC4xNzMwNjE1NzMwLjAuMC4w&amp;amp;_ga=2.239328515.1051314273.1730615731-260007957.1689688404\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Windows process injection overview&lt;/a> written by Amit Klein and Itzik Kotler of SafeBreach, and aim to provide a comprehensive documentation of Linux process injection. We will focus on “true process injection” — techniques that target live, running processes. This means we will exclude methods that require &lt;a href=\&#34;https://violentbinary.github.io/posts/1-elf-static-injection-to-load-malicious-dynamic-link-library/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>modifying the binary on the disk&lt;/a>, &lt;a href=\&#34;https://sumit-ghosh.com/posts/hijacking-library-functions-code-injection-ld-preload/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>executing the process with specific environment variables&lt;/a>, or &lt;a href=\&#34;https://xavibel.com/2022/09/06/linux-shared-library-hijacking/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>abusing the process loading process&lt;/a>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We will describe the OS features that facilitate process injection in Linux, and the different injection primitives they allow. We will cover techniques that have been previously described, and also &lt;b>highlight injection variants that were previously not documented&lt;/b>. We will conclude by covering detection and mitigation strategies for the highlighted techniques.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In addition to this blog post, we are releasing a GitHub &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/akamai/Linux-Process-Injection\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>repository&lt;/a> containing a comprehensive set of proof-of-concept (PoC) code for the different injection primitives described in the post. These benign PoCs are meant to help understand what a malicious implementation of the techniques might look like, which can help you build and test detection capabilities. For additional information, please refer to the project &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/akamai/Linux-Process-Injection/blob/main/README.md\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>README&lt;/a>.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Process injection techniques are an important part of an attacker's toolset. They can enable threat actors to run malicious code inside a legitimate process to avoid detection, or to place hooks in remote processes to modify their behavior. </p>
<p>The topic of process injection on Windows machines has been extensively researched, and there is relatively good awareness of it. For Linux machines, this is not exactly the case. Although some great <a href="https://jm33.me/process-injection-on-linux.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">resources</a> have been <a href="https://joev.dev/posts/unprivileged-process-injection-techniques-in-linux" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">written</a> on the <a href="https://www.aon.com/cyber-solutions/aon_cyber_labs/linux-based-inter-process-code-injection-without-ptrace2/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">topic</a>, awareness of the different injection techniques on Linux seems to be relatively low — especially when compared with Windows.</p>
<p>We drew inspiration from a <a href="https://i.blackhat.com/USA-19/Thursday/us-19-Kotler-Process-Injection-Techniques-Gotta-Catch-Them-All-wp.pdf?_gl=1*ci4ouq*_gcl_au*MTEyMTMyMTU4NC4xNzMwNjE1NzMw*_ga*MjYwMDA3OTU3LjE2ODk2ODg0MDQ.*_ga_K4JK67TFYV*MTczMDYxNTczMC4yNzQuMC4xNzMwNjE1NzMwLjAuMC4w&amp;_ga=2.239328515.1051314273.1730615731-260007957.1689688404" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Windows process injection overview</a> written by Amit Klein and Itzik Kotler of SafeBreach, and aim to provide a comprehensive documentation of Linux process injection. We will focus on “true process injection” — techniques that target live, running processes. This means we will exclude methods that require <a href="https://violentbinary.github.io/posts/1-elf-static-injection-to-load-malicious-dynamic-link-library/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">modifying the binary on the disk</a>, <a href="https://sumit-ghosh.com/posts/hijacking-library-functions-code-injection-ld-preload/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">executing the process with specific environment variables</a>, or <a href="https://xavibel.com/2022/09/06/linux-shared-library-hijacking/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">abusing the process loading process</a>.</p>
<p>We will describe the OS features that facilitate process injection in Linux, and the different injection primitives they allow. We will cover techniques that have been previously described, and also <b>highlight injection variants that were previously not documented</b>. We will conclude by covering detection and mitigation strategies for the highlighted techniques.</p>
<p>In addition to this blog post, we are releasing a GitHub <a href="https://github.com/akamai/Linux-Process-Injection" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">repository</a> containing a comprehensive set of proof-of-concept (PoC) code for the different injection primitives described in the post. These benign PoCs are meant to help understand what a malicious implementation of the techniques might look like, which can help you build and test detection capabilities. For additional information, please refer to the project <a href="https://github.com/akamai/Linux-Process-Injection/blob/main/README.md" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">README</a>.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-a28b955f4f" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-a28b955f4f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:37:06Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Linux injection vs. Windows injection&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Linux injection vs. Windows injection<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-8475d35e4f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:44:09Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The number of known injection techniques on Windows machines is huge, and keeps growing — &lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.ired.team/offensive-security/code-injection-process-injection/apc-queue-code-injection\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>from APC queues&lt;/a> and &lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.ired.team/offensive-security/code-injection-process-injection/process-doppelganging\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>NTFS transactions&lt;/a> to &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/BreakingMalwareResearch/atom-bombing\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>atom tables&lt;/a> and &lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.safebreach.com/blog/process-injection-using-windows-thread-pools/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>thread pools&lt;/a>. Windows exposes many interfaces that enable attackers to interact with (and inject to) remote processes.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The situation is much different in the realm of Linux. Interaction with remote processes is limited to a small set of system calls, and many features that facilitate injection on Windows machines are nowhere to be found. No APIs exist for &lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/api/memoryapi/nf-memoryapi-virtualallocex\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>allocating memory in a remote process&lt;/a> or &lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/api/memoryapi/nf-memoryapi-virtualprotectex\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>modifying remote memory protection&lt;/a>, and definitely not for &lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/api/processthreadsapi/nf-processthreadsapi-createremotethread\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>creating remote threads&lt;/a>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>This difference impacts the structure of the injection attack. In Windows, process injection typically consists of three steps: allocate → write → execute. First, we allocate memory in the remote process that will be used to store our code, then we write our code into this memory, and, finally, we execute it.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>With Linux, we lack the ability to perform the first step — allocation. There is no direct way to allocate memory in a remote process. Because of that, the injection flow will be slightly different: overwrite → execute → recover. We overwrite &lt;b>existing memory&lt;/b> in the remote process with our payload, execute it, and then recover the previous state of the process to allow it to continue executing normally.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The number of known injection techniques on Windows machines is huge, and keeps growing — <a href="https://www.ired.team/offensive-security/code-injection-process-injection/apc-queue-code-injection" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">from APC queues</a> and <a href="https://www.ired.team/offensive-security/code-injection-process-injection/process-doppelganging" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">NTFS transactions</a> to <a href="https://github.com/BreakingMalwareResearch/atom-bombing" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">atom tables</a> and <a href="https://www.safebreach.com/blog/process-injection-using-windows-thread-pools/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">thread pools</a>. Windows exposes many interfaces that enable attackers to interact with (and inject to) remote processes.</p>
<p>The situation is much different in the realm of Linux. Interaction with remote processes is limited to a small set of system calls, and many features that facilitate injection on Windows machines are nowhere to be found. No APIs exist for <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/api/memoryapi/nf-memoryapi-virtualallocex" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">allocating memory in a remote process</a> or <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/api/memoryapi/nf-memoryapi-virtualprotectex" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">modifying remote memory protection</a>, and definitely not for <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/api/processthreadsapi/nf-processthreadsapi-createremotethread" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">creating remote threads</a>.</p>
<p>This difference impacts the structure of the injection attack. In Windows, process injection typically consists of three steps: allocate → write → execute. First, we allocate memory in the remote process that will be used to store our code, then we write our code into this memory, and, finally, we execute it.</p>
<p>With Linux, we lack the ability to perform the first step — allocation. There is no direct way to allocate memory in a remote process. Because of that, the injection flow will be slightly different: overwrite → execute → recover. We overwrite <b>existing memory</b> in the remote process with our payload, execute it, and then recover the previous state of the process to allow it to continue executing normally.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-b799c491d5" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-b799c491d5&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:44:46Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Remote process interaction methods&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Remote process interaction methods<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-65672b7533&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:45:34Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>In Linux, interaction with the memory of remote processes is limited to three main methods: &lt;i>ptrace&lt;/i>, &lt;i>procfs&lt;/i>, and &lt;i>process_vm_writev&lt;/i>. The following sections provide brief descriptions for each of them.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>In Linux, interaction with the memory of remote processes is limited to three main methods: <i>ptrace</i>, <i>procfs</i>, and <i>process_vm_writev</i>. The following sections provide brief descriptions for each of them.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-90bc7b83dd" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-90bc7b83dd&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:45:50Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;ptrace&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">ptrace<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-d1705b6ab9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:46:52Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/ptrace.2.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>ptrace&lt;/a> is a system call used to debug remote processes. The initiating process is able to inspect and modify the debugged process memory and registers. Debuggers like GDB are implemented using ptrace to control the debugged process.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>ptrace supports different operations, which are specified by a &lt;i>ptrace&lt;/i> request code — a few notable examples include PTRACE_ATTACH (which attaches to a process), PTRACE_PEEKTEXT (that reads from the process memory) and PTRACE_GETREGS (which retrieves the process registers). Snippet 1 shows an example use of ptrace.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/ptrace.2.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">ptrace</a> is a system call used to debug remote processes. The initiating process is able to inspect and modify the debugged process memory and registers. Debuggers like GDB are implemented using ptrace to control the debugged process.</p>
<p>ptrace supports different operations, which are specified by a <i>ptrace</i> request code — a few notable examples include PTRACE_ATTACH (which attaches to a process), PTRACE_PEEKTEXT (that reads from the process memory) and PTRACE_GETREGS (which retrieves the process registers). Snippet 1 shows an example use of ptrace.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-e71c9c2e98&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:47:39Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">// Attach to the remote process
  ptrace(PTRACE_ATTACH, pid, NULL, NULL);
  wait(NULL);

  // Get registers state
  struct user_regs_struct regs;
  ptrace(PTRACE_GETREGS, pid, NULL, &amp;regs);</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-688d9b6994&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:48:27Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Snippet 1: Example use of ptrace to retrieve the registers of a remote process&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Snippet 1: Example use of ptrace to retrieve the registers of a remote process</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-a1a1822288" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-a1a1822288&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:48:47Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;procfs&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">procfs<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-c3e33bfa1e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-12T23:49:37Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man5/proc.5.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>procfs&lt;/a> is a special pseudo filesystem that acts as an interface to running processes on the system. It can be accessed through the /proc directory (Figure 1).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man5/proc.5.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">procfs</a> is a special pseudo filesystem that acts as an interface to running processes on the system. It can be accessed through the /proc directory (Figure 1).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="procfs is a special pseudo filesystem that acts as an interface to running processes on the system. It can be accessed through the /proc directory (Figure 1)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-a3a37bf86e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:14:56Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;procfs is a special pseudo filesystem that acts as an interface to running processes on the system. It can be accessed through the /proc directory (Figure 1).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;209b3b4d-c882-48ae-82cc-8c62fdc5fde7&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:14:45Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-one.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-one.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="procfs is a special pseudo filesystem that acts as an interface to running processes on the system. It can be accessed through the /proc directory (Figure 1)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 1: A directory listing of the /proc directory on a Linux machine</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-438dd681f3&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:16:32Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Each process is represented as a directory, named according to its PID. Under this directory we can find files that provide information about the process. For example, the &lt;i>cmdline&lt;/i> file holds the process command line, the &lt;i>environ&lt;/i> file contains the process environment variables, and so forth.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>procfs also provides us with the ability to interact with remote process memory. Inside every process directory we will find the &lt;i>mem&lt;/i> file, a special file that represents the entire address space of the process. Accessing the mem file of a process at a given offset is equivalent to accessing the process memory at the same address.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In the example in Figure 2, we used the xxd utility to read 100 bytes from the process mem file, starting at a specified offset.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Each process is represented as a directory, named according to its PID. Under this directory we can find files that provide information about the process. For example, the <i>cmdline</i> file holds the process command line, the <i>environ</i> file contains the process environment variables, and so forth.</p>
<p>procfs also provides us with the ability to interact with remote process memory. Inside every process directory we will find the <i>mem</i> file, a special file that represents the entire address space of the process. Accessing the mem file of a process at a given offset is equivalent to accessing the process memory at the same address.</p>
<p>In the example in Figure 2, we used the xxd utility to read 100 bytes from the process mem file, starting at a specified offset.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">

    <p>The maps file is another interesting file that can be found in the process directory (Figure 4). This file contains information about the different memory regions in the process address space, including their address ranges and memory permissions.</p>

<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-6e7d6b965a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:22:21Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>In the upcoming sections, we will see how the ability to identify memory regions with specific permissions can be very useful.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>In the upcoming sections, we will see how the ability to identify memory regions with specific permissions can be very useful.</p>

<div class="cmp-title" id="title-bfca22c119" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-bfca22c119&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:22:43Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;process_vm_writev&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">process_vm_writev<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-929f89ef57&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T03:09:42Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The third method to interact with remote process memory is the &lt;a href=\&#34;https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/process_vm_writev.2.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;i>process_vm_writev&lt;/i>&lt;/a> system call. This syscall allows writing data to the address space of a remote process.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>process_vm_writev receives a pointer to a local buffer and copies its contents to a specified address inside the remote process. An example of process_vm_writev in use is shown in Snippet 2.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The third method to interact with remote process memory is the <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/process_vm_writev.2.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer"><i>process_vm_writev</i></a> system call. This syscall allows writing data to the address space of a remote process.</p>
<p>process_vm_writev receives a pointer to a local buffer and copies its contents to a specified address inside the remote process. An example of process_vm_writev in use is shown in Snippet 2.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-e84b944488&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:24:24Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">// Initialize local and remote iovec structs used to perform the syscall
  struct iovec local[1];
  struct iovec remote[1];

  // Place our data in the local iovec 
  local[0].iov_base = data;
  local[0].iov_len = data_len;

  // Point the remote iovec to the address in the remote process
  remote[0].iov_base = (void *)remote_address;
  remote[0].iov_len = data_len;

  // Write the local data to the remote address
  process_vm_writev(pid, local, 1, remote, 1, 0);</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>

<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-f83d86d08f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:24:53Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Snippet 2: Using process_vm_writev to write data to a remote process&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Snippet 2: Using process_vm_writev to write data to a remote process</p>

</div>

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-dac46bca72" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-dac46bca72&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:25:11Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Writing code to a remote process&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Writing code to a remote process<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-0abec1f393&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:25:55Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Now that we understand the different methods to interact with other processes, let&#39;s see how they can be used to perform code injection. The first step of the injection attack will be to write our shellcode into the remote process memory. As we mentioned, in Linux there is no direct way to allocate new memory in a remote process. This means that we can’t create a new memory section; we’ll have to utilize the existing memory of the target process.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>For our code to be able to run, we will need to write it to a memory region with execute permissions. We can find such a region by parsing the previously mentioned procfs maps file, and identifying a memory region with execute (x) permissions (Figure 5).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Now that we understand the different methods to interact with other processes, let's see how they can be used to perform code injection. The first step of the injection attack will be to write our shellcode into the remote process memory. As we mentioned, in Linux there is no direct way to allocate new memory in a remote process. This means that we can’t create a new memory section; we’ll have to utilize the existing memory of the target process.</p>
<p>For our code to be able to run, we will need to write it to a memory region with execute permissions. We can find such a region by parsing the previously mentioned procfs maps file, and identifying a memory region with execute (x) permissions (Figure 5).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="We can find such a region by parsing the previously mentioned procfs maps file, and identifying a memory region with execute (x) permissions (Figure 5)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-dd4c7b5ce8&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:31:13Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;We can find such a region by parsing the previously mentioned procfs maps file, and identifying a memory region with execute (x) permissions (Figure 5).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;13124969-8230-4f34-8338-c84fdaa7ea27&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:31:01Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-five.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-five.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="We can find such a region by parsing the previously mentioned procfs maps file, and identifying a memory region with execute (x) permissions (Figure 5)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 5: Identifying an executable memory region in the process maps file</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-3f8d998f53&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:31:38Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>There are two types of executable regions that we might encounter: writable and non-writable. The following sections will show when and how each of them can be used.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>There are two types of executable regions that we might encounter: writable and non-writable. The following sections will show when and how each of them can be used.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-e62d5ea059" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-e62d5ea059&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:31:55Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Writing code to RX memory&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Writing code to RX memory<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-aee372d1cf&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:33:22Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;b>Applicable to&lt;/b>: ptrace, procfs mem&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Ideally, we will want to identify a memory region with write and execute permissions, which would allow us to write our code and execute it. In reality, most processes will not have a region with such permissions, as it is considered a bad practice to allocate WX memory. Instead, we will usually be limited to read and execute permissions.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Interestingly, it turns out that this limitation can be subverted using two of the methods that we just described — ptrace and procfs mem. Both of these mechanisms are implemented in a way that allows them to bypass memory permissions and write to any address&lt;b>, even without write permissions&lt;/b>. Additional details on this behavior for procfs can be found in &lt;a href=\&#34;https://offlinemark.com/an-obscure-quirk-of-proc/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>this blog post&lt;/a>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>This means that, regardless of write permissions, we can always use ptrace or procfs mem to write our code into a remote executable memory region.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><b>Applicable to</b>: ptrace, procfs mem</p>
<p>Ideally, we will want to identify a memory region with write and execute permissions, which would allow us to write our code and execute it. In reality, most processes will not have a region with such permissions, as it is considered a bad practice to allocate WX memory. Instead, we will usually be limited to read and execute permissions.</p>
<p>Interestingly, it turns out that this limitation can be subverted using two of the methods that we just described — ptrace and procfs mem. Both of these mechanisms are implemented in a way that allows them to bypass memory permissions and write to any address<b>, even without write permissions</b>. Additional details on this behavior for procfs can be found in <a href="https://offlinemark.com/an-obscure-quirk-of-proc/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">this blog post</a>.</p>
<p>This means that, regardless of write permissions, we can always use ptrace or procfs mem to write our code into a remote executable memory region.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-0f46e337e9" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-0f46e337e9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:33:52Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;ptrace&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h4 class="cmp-title__text">ptrace<br />
</h4>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-2768fe7868&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:34:16Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>To write our payload to a remote process we can use the POKETEXT or POKEDATA ptrace requests — these identical requests enable writing a word of data to the remote process memory. By repeatedly calling them we can copy our entire payload into the target process memory. An example of this is shown in Snippet 3.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>To write our payload to a remote process we can use the POKETEXT or POKEDATA ptrace requests — these identical requests enable writing a word of data to the remote process memory. By repeatedly calling them we can copy our entire payload into the target process memory. An example of this is shown in Snippet 3.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-96dbdb842d&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:35:19Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">ptrace(PTRACE_ATTACH, pid, NULL, NULL);
  wait(NULL);

  // write payload to remote address
  for (size_t i = 0; i &lt; payload_size; i += 8, payload++) 
  {
    ptrace(PTRACE_POKETEXT, pid, address + i, *payload);
  }</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-21ceb9bd3a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:35:45Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Snippet 3: Using ptrace POKETEXT to write our payload to the remote process memory&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Snippet 3: Using ptrace POKETEXT to write our payload to the remote process memory</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-42f6ff3bbe" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-42f6ff3bbe&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:36:04Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;procfs mem&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h4 class="cmp-title__text">procfs mem<br />
</h4>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-6883d12ade&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:36:20Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>To write our payload to a remote process using procfs, we simply need to write it to the mem file at the correct offset. Any change that is made to the mem file is applied to the process memory. To perform these operations, we can use the normal file APIs (Snippet 4).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>To write our payload to a remote process using procfs, we simply need to write it to the mem file at the correct offset. Any change that is made to the mem file is applied to the process memory. To perform these operations, we can use the normal file APIs (Snippet 4).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-52a86935b8&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:36:58Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">// Open the process mem file
  FILE *file = fopen(&#34;/proc/&lt;pid&gt;/mem&#34;, &#34;w&#34;);

  // Set the file index to our required offset, representing the memory address
  fseek(file, address, SEEK_SET);

  // Write our payload to the mem file
  fwrite(payload, sizeof(char), payload_size, file);</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-5d610e6a5e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:37:27Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Snippet 4: Using the procfs mem file to write data to a remote process memory&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Snippet 4: Using the procfs mem file to write data to a remote process memory</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-eee43a4ec7" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-eee43a4ec7&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:37:47Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Write code to WX memory&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Write code to WX memory<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-1d151488c2&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:38:29Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;b>Applicable to&lt;/b>: ptrace, procfs mem, process_vm_writev&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>As we’ve discussed, both ptrace and procfs mem bypass memory permissions and enable us to write our code to non-writable memory regions. With process_vm_writev, however, this is not the case. process_vm_writev adheres to memory permissions and therefore only allows us to write data to writable memory regions.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Because of this, our only option is to look for writable regions. Not all processes will contain such regions, but we can certainly find ones that do.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The command in Snippet 5 will scan the maps file of all processes on the system and identify regions with write and execute permissions (Figure 6).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><b>Applicable to</b>: ptrace, procfs mem, process_vm_writev</p>
<p>As we’ve discussed, both ptrace and procfs mem bypass memory permissions and enable us to write our code to non-writable memory regions. With process_vm_writev, however, this is not the case. process_vm_writev adheres to memory permissions and therefore only allows us to write data to writable memory regions.</p>
<p>Because of this, our only option is to look for writable regions. Not all processes will contain such regions, but we can certainly find ones that do.</p>
<p>The command in Snippet 5 will scan the maps file of all processes on the system and identify regions with write and execute permissions (Figure 6).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-11da0ba925&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:38:47Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">find /proc -type f -wholename &#34;*/maps&#34; -exec grep -l &#34;wx&#34; {} +</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>

    <p>Snippet 5: Using the “find” command to identify processes with write and execute memory regions</p>

<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-b4eca69a4d&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:43:08Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>After identifying such a region, we can use process_vm_writev to write our code into it (Snippet 6).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>After identifying such a region, we can use process_vm_writev to write our code into it (Snippet 6).</p>

</div>

<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-d8f9197bb6&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:56:24Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">// Initialize local and remote iovec structs used to perform the syscall
  struct iovec local[1];
  struct iovec remote[1];

  // Place our payload in the local iovec 
  local[0].iov_base = payload;
  local[0].iov_len = payload_len;

  // Point the remote iovec to the address of our wx memory region
  remote[0].iov_base = (void *)wx_address;
  remote[0].iov_len = payload_len;

// Write the local data to the remote address
process_vm_writev(pid, local, 1, remote, 1, 0);</code>
</pre>

<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-947afe38bf&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:56:52Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Snippet 6: Using process_vm_writev to write a payload to a remote WX region&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Snippet 6: Using process_vm_writev to write a payload to a remote WX region</p>

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-1bd2b88344" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-1bd2b88344&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:57:27Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Hijacking remote execution flow&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Hijacking remote execution flow<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-1027210bc4&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:59:26Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>After writing our code to the remote process memory we will need to execute it. In the upcoming sections, we will describe different techniques we can use to accomplish that.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Our research focused on amd64 machines. Some small differences might apply for other architectures, but the general concepts should remain the same.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>After writing our code to the remote process memory we will need to execute it. In the upcoming sections, we will describe different techniques we can use to accomplish that.</p>
<p>Our research focused on amd64 machines. Some small differences might apply for other architectures, but the general concepts should remain the same.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-53b407f924" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-53b407f924&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T00:59:43Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Modifying the process instruction pointer&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Modifying the process instruction pointer<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-5148fe2810&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:00:21Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;b>Applicable to&lt;/b>: ptrace&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>When we attach to a process using ptrace, its execution is paused and we are able to inspect and modify the process registers, including the instruction pointer. This can be done using the SETREGS and GETREGS ptrace requests. To modify the execution flow of the process, we can use ptrace to modify the instruction pointer to the address of our shellcode.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In the example in Snippet 7, we performed the following three steps:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ol>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Retrieve the current register values using the GETREGS ptrace request&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Modify the instruction pointer to point to our payload address (incremented by 2, which we will discuss later)&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Apply the change to the process by using the SETREGS request&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ol>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><b>Applicable to</b>: ptrace</p>
<p>When we attach to a process using ptrace, its execution is paused and we are able to inspect and modify the process registers, including the instruction pointer. This can be done using the SETREGS and GETREGS ptrace requests. To modify the execution flow of the process, we can use ptrace to modify the instruction pointer to the address of our shellcode.</p>
<p>In the example in Snippet 7, we performed the following three steps:</p>
<ol>
<li><p>Retrieve the current register values using the GETREGS ptrace request</p>
</li>
<li><p>Modify the instruction pointer to point to our payload address (incremented by 2, which we will discuss later)</p>
</li>
<li><p>Apply the change to the process by using the SETREGS request</p>
</li>
</ol>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-e414bef81f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:00:56Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">// Get old register state.
  struct user_regs_struct regs;
  ptrace(PTRACE_GETREGS, pid, NULL, &amp;regs);
 
  // Modify the instruction pointer to point to our payload
  regs.rip = payload_address + 2;

  // Modify the registers
  ptrace(PTRACE_SETREGS, pid, NULL, &amp;regs);</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-272d54e60a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:04:32Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Snippet 7: Using ptrace SETREGS to point the instruction pointer to our payload&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Snippet 7: Using ptrace SETREGS to point the instruction pointer to our payload</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-262c6bcb1b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:02:14Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>SETREGS is the “traditional” and most documented way to modify the process registers, but another ptrace request can also be used to accomplish this — POKEUSER.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The POKEUSER request enables writing data to the process &lt;i>USER&lt;/i> &lt;i>area&lt;/i> — a structure (defined in &lt;a href=\&#34;https://sites.uclouvain.be/SystInfo/usr/include/sys/user.h.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>sys/user.h&lt;/a>) that contains information about the process, including the registers. By calling POKEUSER with the correct offset, we can overwrite the instruction pointer with the address of our code and achieve the same result as before (Snippet 8).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>SETREGS is the “traditional” and most documented way to modify the process registers, but another ptrace request can also be used to accomplish this — POKEUSER.</p>
<p>The POKEUSER request enables writing data to the process <i>USER</i> <i>area</i> — a structure (defined in <a href="https://sites.uclouvain.be/SystInfo/usr/include/sys/user.h.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">sys/user.h</a>) that contains information about the process, including the registers. By calling POKEUSER with the correct offset, we can overwrite the instruction pointer with the address of our code and achieve the same result as before (Snippet 8).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-26f5866153&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:06:24Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">// calculate the offset of the RIP register, based on the USER struct definition
  rip_offset = 16 * sizeof(unsigned long);
  ptrace(PTRACE_POKEUSER, pid, rip_offset, payload_address + 2);</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-a40e6101e0&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:07:29Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Snippet 8: Using ptrace POKEUSER to point the instruction pointer to our payload&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Our implementation of using POKEUSER to modify RIP can be &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/guardicode/linux_injection_examples/blob/main/src/ptrace_primitives.c#L69\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>found in our repository&lt;/a>.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Snippet 8: Using ptrace POKEUSER to point the instruction pointer to our payload</p>
<p>Our implementation of using POKEUSER to modify RIP can be <a href="https://github.com/guardicode/linux_injection_examples/blob/main/src/ptrace_primitives.c#L69" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">found in our repository</a>.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-afe5c0a6a3" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-afe5c0a6a3&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T14:05:22Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;RIP += 2: When and why?&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">RIP += 2: When and why?<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-64b7948177&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T14:05:07Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>As shown in Snippet 7 and Snippet 8, when we modify RIP to the address of our payload we are also incrementing it by 2. This is done to accommodate for an &lt;a href=\&#34;https://stackoverflow.com/questions/38006277/weird-behavior-setting-rip-with-ptrace\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>interesting ptrace behavior&lt;/a> — sometimes after detaching from a process with ptrace, the value of RIP will be decremented by 2. Let’s understand why this is happening.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>When we attach to a process using ptrace, we may interrupt a syscall that is currently executing in the kernel. To make sure that the syscall executes properly, the kernel will rerun it when we detach from the process.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>While the syscall is executing, RIP already points to the next instruction to be executed. To rerun the syscall, the kernel will decrement the value of RIP by 2 — the size of the syscall instruction in amd64. After this change, RIP will point to the syscall instruction again, causing it to run another time (Figure 7).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>As shown in Snippet 7 and Snippet 8, when we modify RIP to the address of our payload we are also incrementing it by 2. This is done to accommodate for an <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/questions/38006277/weird-behavior-setting-rip-with-ptrace" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">interesting ptrace behavior</a> — sometimes after detaching from a process with ptrace, the value of RIP will be decremented by 2. Let’s understand why this is happening.</p>
<p>When we attach to a process using ptrace, we may interrupt a syscall that is currently executing in the kernel. To make sure that the syscall executes properly, the kernel will rerun it when we detach from the process.</p>
<p>While the syscall is executing, RIP already points to the next instruction to be executed. To rerun the syscall, the kernel will decrement the value of RIP by 2 — the size of the syscall instruction in amd64. After this change, RIP will point to the syscall instruction again, causing it to run another time (Figure 7).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="After this change, RIP will point to the syscall instruction again, causing it to run another time (Figure 7)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-be60092c2e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:15:36Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;After this change, RIP will point to the syscall instruction again, causing it to run another time (Figure 7).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;2ed16cb6-98e5-4268-aa47-5e8fbf405edf&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:15:23Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-seven.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-seven.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="After this change, RIP will point to the syscall instruction again, causing it to run another time (Figure 7)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 7: The effect of using ptrace on a process during syscall execution</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-e26dd6eaf6&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:16:37Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>If we happen to interrupt a process during a syscall when performing code injection, problems can occur. After we modify RIP to point to our code, the kernel will still decrement the new value by 2, leading to a 2-byte gap before our shellcode, which will likely cause it to fail (Figure 8).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>If we happen to interrupt a process during a syscall when performing code injection, problems can occur. After we modify RIP to point to our code, the kernel will still decrement the new value by 2, leading to a 2-byte gap before our shellcode, which will likely cause it to fail (Figure 8).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="After we modify RIP to point to our code, the kernel will still decrement the new value by 2, leading to a 2-byte gap before our shellcode, which will likely cause it to fail (Figure 8)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-0b8bfebff9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:20:26Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;After we modify RIP to point to our code, the kernel will still decrement the new value by 2, leading to a 2-byte gap before our shellcode, which will likely cause it to fail (Figure 8).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;922744ca-9237-4643-a964-3d079c2eb2a7&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:18:37Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-eight.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-eight.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="After we modify RIP to point to our code, the kernel will still decrement the new value by 2, leading to a 2-byte gap before our shellcode, which will likely cause it to fail (Figure 8)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 8: Using ptrace to point RIP to our shellcode results in a junk instruction executing</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-abe7bd8333&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:20:58Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>To accommodate for this behavior, we will take two actions: prefix our shellcode with two no operation (NOP) instructions, and point RIP to the address of our shellcode + 2. These two steps will make sure our code executes properly.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>If we interrupted the process during a syscall, the kernel will decrement the new RIP value, which will result in it pointing to the start address of the shellcode that contains two NOPs that we will slide into our actual code.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>If we didn’t interrupt the process during a syscall, the new RIP will not be decremented, which will result in the two NOPs being skipped and our code executing. These 2 scenarios are depicted in Figure 9.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>To accommodate for this behavior, we will take two actions: prefix our shellcode with two no operation (NOP) instructions, and point RIP to the address of our shellcode + 2. These two steps will make sure our code executes properly.</p>
<p>If we interrupted the process during a syscall, the kernel will decrement the new RIP value, which will result in it pointing to the start address of the shellcode that contains two NOPs that we will slide into our actual code.</p>
<p>If we didn’t interrupt the process during a syscall, the new RIP will not be decremented, which will result in the two NOPs being skipped and our code executing. These 2 scenarios are depicted in Figure 9.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="These 2 scenarios are depicted in Figure 9" class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-313a4d2868&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:22:36Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;These 2 scenarios are depicted in Figure 9&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;cf1535d2-22cb-4eb4-965e-2ed8650039fb&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:22:26Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-nine.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-nine.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="These 2 scenarios are depicted in Figure 9"/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 9: Overcoming the ptrace RIP interaction</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-0448834a2c" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-0448834a2c&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:24:35Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Modify current instruction&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Modify current instruction<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-f30d2fb335&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:26:46Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;b>Applicable to&lt;/b>: ptrace, procfs mem&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Another interesting file in procfs is the &lt;a href=\&#34;https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man5/proc.5.html#:~:text=/proc/pid/syscall%20(since%20Linux%202.6.27)\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;i>syscall&lt;/i>&lt;/a> file. This file holds information about the syscall that is currently executed by the process — the syscall number, the arguments that were passed to it, the stack pointer, and (most interesting for our cause) the process instruction pointer (Figure 10). Even if the process is not currently executing a syscall, the stack and instruction pointers of the process will still be present in the syscall file.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><b>Applicable to</b>: ptrace, procfs mem</p>
<p>Another interesting file in procfs is the <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man5/proc.5.html#:~:text=/proc/pid/syscall%20(since%20Linux%202.6.27)" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer"><i>syscall</i></a> file. This file holds information about the syscall that is currently executed by the process — the syscall number, the arguments that were passed to it, the stack pointer, and (most interesting for our cause) the process instruction pointer (Figure 10). Even if the process is not currently executing a syscall, the stack and instruction pointers of the process will still be present in the syscall file.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="Another interesting file in procfs is the syscall file. This file holds information about the syscall that is currently executed by the process — the syscall number, the arguments that were passed to it, the stack pointer, and (most interesting for our cause) the process instruction pointer (Figure 10)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-ddf6998574&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:28:40Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Another interesting file in procfs is the syscall file. This file holds information about the syscall that is currently executed by the process — the syscall number, the arguments that were passed to it, the stack pointer, and (most interesting for our cause) the process instruction pointer (Figure 10).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;71883804-6fe4-4da5-86da-c0e46e1c15bd&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:28:28Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-ten.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-ten.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="Another interesting file in procfs is the syscall file. This file holds information about the syscall that is currently executed by the process — the syscall number, the arguments that were passed to it, the stack pointer, and (most interesting for our cause) the process instruction pointer (Figure 10)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 10: The structure of the procfs syscall file</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-97a3234df2&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:30:41Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>This information can allow us to take control over the execution flow of the process; knowing the address of the next instruction to be executed allows us to overwrite it with our own instructions.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>To implement this, an attacker can perform the following four steps:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ol>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Stop the process execution by sending a SIGSTOP signal&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Identify the address of the next instruction to be executed by reading the process syscall file&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Write shellcode to the identified address&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Resume process execution by sending a SIGCONT signal&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ol>\r\n&lt;p>Snippet 9 provides a pseudo code for this process.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>This information can allow us to take control over the execution flow of the process; knowing the address of the next instruction to be executed allows us to overwrite it with our own instructions.</p>
<p>To implement this, an attacker can perform the following four steps:</p>
<ol>
<li><p>Stop the process execution by sending a SIGSTOP signal</p>
</li>
<li><p>Identify the address of the next instruction to be executed by reading the process syscall file</p>
</li>
<li><p>Write shellcode to the identified address</p>
</li>
<li><p>Resume process execution by sending a SIGCONT signal</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Snippet 9 provides a pseudo code for this process.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-e4af47dc26&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:32:53Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">// Suspend the process by sending a SIGSTOP signal
  kill(pid, SIGSTOP);

  // Open the syscall file
  FILE *syscall_file = fopen(&#34;/proc/&lt;pid&gt;/syscall&#34;, &#34;r&#34;);

  // Extract the instruction pointer from the syscall file
  long instruction_pointer = ... 

  // Write our payload to the address of the current instruction pointer using 
  procfs mem
  FILE *mem_file = fopen(&#34;/proc/&lt;pid&gt;/mem&#34;, &#34;w&#34;);
  fseek(mem_file, instruction_pointer, SEEK_SET);
  fwrite(payload, sizeof(char), payload_size, mem_file);

  // Resume execution by sending a SIGCONT signal
  kill(pid, SIGCONT);</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-8286abe47e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:33:35Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Snippet 9: Using procfs mem to modify the process memory at the current address of the instruction pointer to hijack the execution flow of the process&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Snippet 9: Using procfs mem to modify the process memory at the current address of the instruction pointer to hijack the execution flow of the process</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-2f7bbcb565&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:34:06Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The example in Snippet 9 implements this technique using the procfs mem file, but it is important to note that ptrace POKETEXT can also be used to write the payload to memory.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>As we’ve mentioned, process_vm_writev is limited by memory permissions, meaning it can only modify writable memory regions. The likelihood of finding code running from a WX memory region is low, which reduces the reliability of process_vm_writev for this primitive.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/guardicode/linux_injection_examples/blob/main/src/procfs_primitives.c#L37\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Check out&lt;/a> our implementation of this technique using the procfs mem file.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The example in Snippet 9 implements this technique using the procfs mem file, but it is important to note that ptrace POKETEXT can also be used to write the payload to memory.</p>
<p>As we’ve mentioned, process_vm_writev is limited by memory permissions, meaning it can only modify writable memory regions. The likelihood of finding code running from a WX memory region is low, which reduces the reliability of process_vm_writev for this primitive.</p>
<p><a href="https://github.com/guardicode/linux_injection_examples/blob/main/src/procfs_primitives.c#L37" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Check out</a> our implementation of this technique using the procfs mem file.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-bedbde0322" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-bedbde0322&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:35:09Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Stack hijacking&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Stack hijacking<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-53b904bd85&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:35:41Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;b>Applicable to&lt;/b>: ptrace, procfs mem file, process_vm_writev&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Another interesting memory region is the process stack, which can also be identified using the maps file. Although the stack memory is not executable (Figure 11), we can still use it to hijack the execution flow of the process.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><b>Applicable to</b>: ptrace, procfs mem file, process_vm_writev</p>
<p>Another interesting memory region is the process stack, which can also be identified using the maps file. Although the stack memory is not executable (Figure 11), we can still use it to hijack the execution flow of the process.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="Although the stack memory is not executable (Figure 11), we can still use it to hijack the execution flow of the process." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-518f08a330&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:38:43Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Although the stack memory is not executable (Figure 11), we can still use it to hijack the execution flow of the process.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;31806086-c7b6-4604-a4a3-ca6df225cb56&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:36:48Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-eleven.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/the-definitive-guide-to-linux-process-injection-eleven.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="Although the stack memory is not executable (Figure 11), we can still use it to hijack the execution flow of the process."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 11: Identifying the process stack address using the maps file</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-2505ba1373&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-11-13T01:41:21Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Whenever a function is called, the return address of the calling function is pushed to the stack. When the function finishes execution, the processor takes this return address from the stack and jumps to it (Figure 12).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Whenever a function is called, the return address of the calling function is pushed to the stack. When the function finishes execution, the processor takes this return address from the stack and jumps to it (Figure 12).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="When the function finishes execution, the processor takes this return address from the stack and jumps to it (Figure 12).
